Here's how the chain works:\\n\\n**1. Style Change Notification (layout/style/RestyleManager)**\\nWhen a CSS property changes (via style attribute modification, class changes, etc.), RestyleManager::PostRestyleEvent() is called. This function (RestyleManager.h:315) queues a restyle request by calling Servo_NoteExplicitHints() to mark the element for style recomputation. The restyle event is queued rather than applied immediately, allowing batching of multiple style changes.\\n\\n**2. Frame Style Recomputation (layout/style/ServoStyleSet)**\\nWhen layout flushes pending notifications, RestyleManager::DoProcessPendingRestyles() (RestyleManager.cpp:3087) invokes ServoStyleSet::StyleDocument() (ServoStyleSet.h:311). This performs the actual CSS style computation using the Servo style engine, traversing the DOM tree and recalculating computed styles. After style computation, RestyleManager::ProcessPostTraversal() (RestyleManager.cpp:2747) walks the frame tree to detect what needs to be updated.\\n\\n**3. For layout-affecting changes, StyleChangeReflow() (RestyleManager.cpp:1326) is called, which invokes PresShell::FrameNeedsReflow() (PresShell.cpp:2632). This function marks frames as dirty (NS_FRAME_IS_DIRTY or NS_FRAME_HAS_DIRTY_CHILDREN state bits) and propagates the dirty state up the frame tree to reflow roots. The reflow will occur during the next flush.\\n\\n**4. This function creates an nsDisplayListBuilder and calls nsIFrame::BuildDisplayListForStackingContext() (line 3191) to recursively construct the display list. For WebRender, this may use RetainedDisplayListBuilder for partial updates or TemporaryDisplayListBuilder for full rebuilds.\\n\\n**5.
